## SC-500

### Manage identity, access, and governance

#### sc500-d1-q01 (easy)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

FortisAid Healthcare is working in a healthcare tenant with sensitive patient data. The security lead needs to secure cloud and AI access continuously. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. combine least privilege, Conditional Access, risk signals, and continuous evaluation
- B. trust corporate network location only
- C. grant standing admin rights
- D. disable sign-in risk policies

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to combine least privilege, Conditional Access, risk signals, and continuous evaluation. This directly addresses Zero Trust and least privilege, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the Zero Trust and least privilege requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Zero Trust and least privilege requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Zero Trust and least privilege requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q02 (medium)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

During a review at ClearVault Finance, auditors found a gap related to Key Vault governance. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. store secrets in source code
- B. use Key Vault RBAC/access controls, firewall or private endpoint, soft delete, purge protection, and Defender for Key Vault
- C. share vault access keys
- D. allow public access from all networks

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Key Vault RBAC/access controls, firewall or private endpoint, soft delete, purge protection, and Defender for Key Vault. This directly addresses Key Vault governance, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Key Vault governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Key Vault governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Key Vault governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q03 (medium)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

A change request at Helix x Pulse Networks says: "enforce security baselines across subscriptions." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. document standards only
- B. use manual screenshots
- C. assign built-in or custom Azure Policy initiatives and remediate non-compliance
- D. make every admin Owner

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to assign built-in or custom Azure Policy initiatives and remediate non-compliance. This directly addresses Azure Policy and compliance, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q04 (hard)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

Nexus Financial has a production issue involving over-privileged access remediation. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. ignore inherited roles
- B. increase all roles to Contributor
- C. turn off audit logs
- D. review role assignments, use PIM/access reviews, and right-size RBAC

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to review role assignments, use PIM/access reviews, and right-size RBAC. This directly addresses over-privileged access remediation, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q05 (medium)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

You are designing controls for FortisAid Healthcare. The requirement is to secure synchronized identities and monitor identity threats. Which implementation is the most appropriate?

- A. harden synchronization, monitor Connect Health, protect privileged accounts, and use Identity Protection
- B. sync all legacy admin accounts without review
- C. disable password protection
- D. bypass Conditional Access for synced users

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to harden synchronization, monitor Connect Health, protect privileged accounts, and use Identity Protection. This directly addresses hybrid identity security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

- C. assign built-in or custom Azure Policy initiatives and remediate non-compliance
- D. make every admin Owner

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to assign built-in or custom Azure Policy initiatives and remediate non-compliance. This directly addresses Azure Policy and compliance, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Azure Policy and compliance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q24 (hard)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

Nexus Financial has a production issue involving over-privileged access remediation. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. ignore inherited roles
- B. increase all roles to Contributor
- C. turn off audit logs
- D. review role assignments, use PIM/access reviews, and right-size RBAC

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to review role assignments, use PIM/access reviews, and right-size RBAC. This directly addresses over-privileged access remediation, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the over-privileged access remediation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d1-q25 (medium)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

You are designing controls for FortisAid Healthcare. The requirement is to secure synchronized identities and monitor identity threats. Which implementation is the most appropriate?

- A. harden synchronization, monitor Connect Health, protect privileged accounts, and use Identity Protection
- B. sync all legacy admin accounts without review
- C. disable password protection
- D. bypass Conditional Access for synced users

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to harden synchronization, monitor Connect Health, protect privileged accounts, and use Identity Protection. This directly addresses hybrid identity security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the hybrid identity security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

- A. trust corporate network location only
- B. combine least privilege, Conditional Access, risk signals, and continuous evaluation
- C. grant standing admin rights
- D. disable sign-in risk policies

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to combine least privilege, Conditional Access, risk signals, and continuous evaluation. This directly addresses Zero Trust and least privilege, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage identity, access, and governance.

### Protect storage, databases, and networks

#### sc500-d2-q01 (easy)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

ClearVault Finance is working in a secure Azure landing zone. The security lead needs to protect sensitive files from public exposure and deletion. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. allow anonymous containers
- B. share account keys broadly
- C. use private access, RBAC, Defender for Storage, soft delete/versioning, and immutable storage
- D. disable blob versioning for critical data

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use private access, RBAC, Defender for Storage, soft delete/versioning, and immutable storage. This directly addresses secure storage, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q02 (medium)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

During a review at Helix x Pulse Networks, auditors found a gap related to secure databases. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. open firewall to 0.0.0.0/0
- B. disable audit retention
- C. use shared SQL logins
- D. enable auditing, Defender for SQL, vulnerability assessment, TDE, data masking, and private access

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to enable auditing, Defender for SQL, vulnerability assessment, TDE, data masking, and private access. This directly addresses secure databases, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the secure databases requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the secure databases requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the secure databases requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q03 (medium)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

A change request at Nexus Financial says: "segment workloads and inspect traffic." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. use NSGs/ASGs, Azure Firewall, Private Endpoints, WAF, and DDoS protection as appropriate
- B. use public endpoints for every service
- C. rely only on naming conventions
- D. grant RBAC instead of network controls

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use NSGs/ASGs, Azure Firewall, Private Endpoints, WAF, and DDoS protection as appropriate. This directly addresses network security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q04 (hard)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

FortisAid Healthcare has a production issue involving private access architecture. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. use service tags as the only control
- B. deploy Private Endpoints and private DNS zones
- C. enable anonymous public access
- D. put secrets in route tables

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to deploy Private Endpoints and private DNS zones. This directly addresses private access architecture, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q05 (medium)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

You are designing controls for ClearVault Finance. The requirement is to identify leaked secrets in cloud assets and code. Which implementation is the most appropriate?

- A. rotate nothing until an incident
- B. ignore old repositories
- C. use Defender CSPM/Defender for Cloud secret scanning and remediate exposed credentials
- D. grant read access to all developers

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Defender CSPM/Defender for Cloud secret scanning and remediate exposed credentials. This directly addresses secret exposure detection, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the secret exposure detection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the secret exposure detection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q06 (easy)

Helix x Pulse Networks is working in a post-acquisition identity consolidation. The security lead needs to protect sensitive files from public exposure and deletion. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. allow anonymous containers
- B. share account keys broadly
- C. disable blob versioning for critical data
- D. use private access, RBAC, Defender for Storage, soft delete/versioning, and immutable storage

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use private access, RBAC, Defender for Storage, soft delete/versioning, and immutable storage. This directly addresses secure storage, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q07 (medium)

- A. enable auditing, Defender for SQL, vulnerability assessment, TDE, data masking, and private access
- B. open firewall to 0.0.0.0/0
- C. disable audit retention
- D. use shared SQL logins

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to enable auditing, Defender for SQL, vulnerability assessment, TDE, data masking, and private access. This directly addresses secure databases, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

- A: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the secure storage requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q37 (medium)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

During a review at ClearVault Finance, auditors found a gap related to secure databases. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. open firewall to 0.0.0.0/0
- B. disable audit retention
- C. enable auditing, Defender for SQL, vulnerability assessment, TDE, data masking, and private access
- D. use shared SQL logins

#### sc500-d2-q38 (medium)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

A change request at Helix x Pulse Networks says: "segment workloads and inspect traffic." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. use public endpoints for every service
- B. rely only on naming conventions
- C. grant RBAC instead of network controls
- D. use NSGs/ASGs, Azure Firewall, Private Endpoints, WAF, and DDoS protection as appropriate

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use NSGs/ASGs, Azure Firewall, Private Endpoints, WAF, and DDoS protection as appropriate. This directly addresses network security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the network security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d2-q39 (hard)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

Nexus Financial has a production issue involving private access architecture. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. deploy Private Endpoints and private DNS zones
- B. use service tags as the only control
- C. enable anonymous public access
- D. put secrets in route tables

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to deploy Private Endpoints and private DNS zones. This directly addresses private access architecture, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Protect storage, databases, and networks. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the private access architecture requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

- A. rotate nothing until an incident
- B. use Defender CSPM/Defender for Cloud secret scanning and remediate exposed credentials
- C. ignore old repositories
- D. grant read access to all developers

**Answer:** B

### Secure compute

#### sc500-d3-q01 (easy)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

Helix x Pulse Networks is working in a post-acquisition identity consolidation. The security lead needs to secure Azure, hybrid, and multi-cloud servers. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. onboard to Defender for Servers, use vulnerability assessment, EDR, JIT, Bastion, and secure boot controls
- B. leave public RDP open
- C. run unmanaged local admin accounts
- D. disable endpoint protection

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to onboard to Defender for Servers, use vulnerability assessment, EDR, JIT, Bastion, and secure boot controls. This directly addresses server and VM protection, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q02 (medium)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

During a review at Nexus Financial, auditors found a gap related to Azure Arc security. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. manage servers separately with no telemetry
- B. onboard servers to Azure Arc and apply Defender for Servers, policy, and monitoring
- C. copy logs manually
- D. use shared local passwords

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to onboard servers to Azure Arc and apply Defender for Servers, policy, and monitoring. This directly addresses Azure Arc security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q03 (medium)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

A change request at FortisAid Healthcare says: "protect clusters and container images." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. run all pods privileged
- B. allow anonymous registry pull
- C. use Defender for Containers, ACR scanning, Kubernetes RBAC, network policies, and managed identity
- D. skip image scanning

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Defender for Containers, ACR scanning, Kubernetes RBAC, network policies, and managed identity. This directly addresses container and AKS security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the container and AKS security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the container and AKS security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the container and AKS security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q04 (hard)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

ClearVault Finance has a production issue involving App Service and API security. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. store API keys in code
- B. disable HTTPS only
- C. use public SCM access from anywhere
- D. use authentication, managed identity, Key Vault references, TLS, private endpoints, and WAF where appropriate

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use authentication, managed identity, Key Vault references, TLS, private endpoints, and WAF where appropriate. This directly addresses App Service and API security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

- A. use Azure Machine Configuration with policy assignments
- B. use a spreadsheet checklist
- C. manually inspect once
- D. disable compliance reporting

**Answer:** A

#### sc500-d3-q19 (hard)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

FortisAid Healthcare has a production issue involving App Service and API security. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. store API keys in code
- B. disable HTTPS only
- C. use authentication, managed identity, Key Vault references, TLS, private endpoints, and WAF where appropriate
- D. use public SCM access from anywhere

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use authentication, managed identity, Key Vault references, TLS, private endpoints, and WAF where appropriate. This directly addresses App Service and API security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the App Service and API security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q20 (medium)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

You are designing controls for ClearVault Finance. The requirement is to enforce guest OS security settings. Which implementation is the most appropriate?

- A. use a spreadsheet checklist
- B. manually inspect once
- C. disable compliance reporting
- D. use Azure Machine Configuration with policy assignments

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Azure Machine Configuration with policy assignments. This directly addresses machine configuration, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the machine configuration requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the machine configuration requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the machine configuration requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q21 (easy)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

Helix x Pulse Networks is working in a post-acquisition identity consolidation. The security lead needs to secure Azure, hybrid, and multi-cloud servers. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. onboard to Defender for Servers, use vulnerability assessment, EDR, JIT, Bastion, and secure boot controls
- B. leave public RDP open
- C. run unmanaged local admin accounts
- D. disable endpoint protection

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to onboard to Defender for Servers, use vulnerability assessment, EDR, JIT, Bastion, and secure boot controls. This directly addresses server and VM protection, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the server and VM protection requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d3-q22 (medium)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

During a review at Nexus Financial, auditors found a gap related to Azure Arc security. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. manage servers separately with no telemetry
- B. onboard servers to Azure Arc and apply Defender for Servers, policy, and monitoring
- C. copy logs manually
- D. use shared local passwords

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to onboard servers to Azure Arc and apply Defender for Servers, policy, and monitoring. This directly addresses Azure Arc security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Azure Arc security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

A change request at FortisAid Healthcare says: "protect clusters and container images." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. run all pods privileged
- B. allow anonymous registry pull
- C. use Defender for Containers, ACR scanning, Kubernetes RBAC, network policies, and managed identity
- D. skip image scanning

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Defender for Containers, ACR scanning, Kubernetes RBAC, network policies, and managed identity. This directly addresses container and AKS security, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Secure compute.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the container and AKS security requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

### Manage and monitor security posture

#### sc500-d4-q01 (easy)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

Nexus Financial is working in a regulated finance environment. The security lead needs to centralize detection, investigation, and response. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. use disconnected spreadsheets
- B. ingest no identity logs
- C. connect data sources, create analytics rules, manage incidents, workbooks, watchlists, and playbooks
- D. disable incident grouping

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to connect data sources, create analytics rules, manage incidents, workbooks, watchlists, and playbooks. This directly addresses Microsoft Sentinel operations, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Sentinel operations requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Sentinel operations requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Sentinel operations requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d4-q02 (medium)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

During a review at FortisAid Healthcare, auditors found a gap related to Microsoft Security Copilot. You must fix it without adding unnecessary standing access. What should you do?

- A. let Copilot take action without review
- B. replace all logging with prompts
- C. disable human approval
- D. use Security Copilot prompts grounded in Defender/Sentinel context and verify recommendations

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use Security Copilot prompts grounded in Defender/Sentinel context and verify recommendations. This directly addresses Microsoft Security Copilot, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Security Copilot requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Security Copilot requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Security Copilot requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d4-q03 (medium)

**Scenario:** ClearVault Finance

A change request at ClearVault Finance says: "find sensitive data exposure that increases AI risk." The solution must be auditable and aligned to Microsoft cloud security practices. Which option should you choose?

- A. use DSPM to identify overshared sensitive data and prioritize remediation
- B. ignore SharePoint exposure
- C. grant Copilot access to all sites
- D. turn off sensitivity labels

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use DSPM to identify overshared sensitive data and prioritize remediation. This directly addresses Microsoft Purview DSPM, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- B: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Purview DSPM requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Purview DSPM requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Microsoft Purview DSPM requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d4-q04 (hard)

**Scenario:** Helix x Pulse Networks

Helix x Pulse Networks has a production issue involving Defender for AI and model endpoints. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. publish model endpoints anonymously
- B. enable appropriate Defender protections and monitor the Data & AI security dashboard
- C. store prompt logs nowhere
- D. disable threat alerts

**Answer:** B

**Explanation:** The best answer is to enable appropriate Defender protections and monitor the Data & AI security dashboard. This directly addresses Defender for AI and model endpoints, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d4-q05 (medium)

**Scenario:** Nexus Financial

You are designing controls for Nexus Financial. The requirement is to control autonomous agents and their permissions. Which implementation is the most appropriate?

- A. give agents broad standing permissions
- B. skip access reviews
- C. govern agent identities, permissions, data access, monitoring, and response workflows
- D. allow unmanaged plugins

**Answer:** C

**Explanation:** The best answer is to govern agent identities, permissions, data access, monitoring, and response workflows. This directly addresses agentic AI governance, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the agentic AI governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the agentic AI governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- D: This does not fully meet the agentic AI governance requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

#### sc500-d4-q06 (easy)

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

FortisAid Healthcare is working in a healthcare tenant with sensitive patient data. The security lead needs to respond consistently to high-confidence incidents. Which action best satisfies the requirement while following least privilege?

- A. auto-delete users without validation
- B. require manual response to every low-risk alert
- C. disable enrichment
- D. use automation rules, playbooks, and approval gates for sensitive actions

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to use automation rules, playbooks, and approval gates for sensitive actions. This directly addresses security automation, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the security automation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the security automation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the security automation requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

**Scenario:** FortisAid Healthcare

FortisAid Healthcare has a production issue involving Defender for AI and model endpoints. The team wants the fastest secure remediation, not a temporary workaround. What is the best answer? The solution must minimize blast radius and preserve investigation evidence.

- A. publish model endpoints anonymously
- B. store prompt logs nowhere
- C. disable threat alerts
- D. enable appropriate Defender protections and monitor the Data & AI security dashboard

**Answer:** D

**Explanation:** The best answer is to enable appropriate Defender protections and monitor the Data & AI security dashboard. This directly addresses Defender for AI and model endpoints, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture. In exam scenarios, prefer controls that are enforceable, auditable, and least-privileged over broad access or manual process.

**Why the others are wrong:**
- A: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- B: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.
- C: This does not fully meet the Defender for AI and model endpoints requirement or creates unnecessary risk.

- A. govern agent identities, permissions, data access, monitoring, and response workflows
- B. give agents broad standing permissions
- C. skip access reviews
- D. allow unmanaged plugins

**Answer:** A

**Explanation:** The best answer is to govern agent identities, permissions, data access, monitoring, and response workflows. This directly addresses agentic AI governance, keeps permissions scoped, and matches the exam objective for Manage and monitor security posture.

- B. use automation rules, playbooks, and approval gates for sensitive actions
